  The OpenStack service that provides services and associated libraries to store, browse, share, distribute and manage bootable disk images, other data closely associated with initializing compute resources, and metadata definitions.

- image status[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-image-status)

  The current status of a VM image in Image service, not to be confused with the status of a running instance.

- image store[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-image-store)

  The back-end store used by Image service to store VM images, options include Object Storage, locally mounted file system, RADOS block devices, VMware datastore, or HTTP.

- image UUID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-image-UUID)

  UUID used by Image service to uniquely identify each VM image.

- incubated project[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-incubated-project)

  A community project may be elevated to this status and is then promoted to a core project.

- Infrastructure Optimization service (watcher)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Infrastructure-Optimization-service-watcher)

  OpenStack project that aims to provide a flexible and scalable resource optimization service for multi-project OpenStack-based clouds.

- Infrastructure-as-a-Service (IaaS)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Infrastructure-as-a-Service-IaaS)

  IaaS is a provisioning model in which an organization outsources physical components of a data center, such as storage, hardware, servers, and networking components. A service provider owns the equipment and is responsible for housing, operating and maintaining it. The client typically pays on a per-use basis. IaaS is a model for providing cloud services.

- ingress filtering[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-ingress-filtering)

  The process of filtering incoming network traffic. Supported by Compute.

- INI format[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-INI-format)

  The OpenStack configuration files use an INI format to describe options and their values. It consists of sections and key value pairs.

- injection[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-injection)

  The process of putting a file into a virtual machine image before the instance is started.

- Input/Output Operations Per Second (IOPS)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Input-Output-Operations-Per-Second-IOPS)

  IOPS are a common performance measurement used to benchmark computer storage devices like hard disk drives, solid state drives, and storage area networks.

- instance[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-instance)

  A running VM, or a VM in a known state such as suspended, that can be used like a hardware server.

- instance ID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-instance-ID)

  Alternative term for instance UUID.

- instance state[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-instance-state)

  The current state of a guest VM image.

- instance tunnels network[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-instance-tunnels-network)

  A network segment used for instance traffic tunnels between compute nodes and the network node.

- instance type[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-instance-type)

  Describes the parameters of the various virtual machine images that are available to users; includes parameters such as CPU, storage, and memory. Alternative term for flavor.

- instance type ID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-instance-type-ID)

  Alternative term for a flavor ID.

- instance UUID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-instance-UUID)

  Unique ID assigned to each guest VM instance.

- Intelligent Platform Management Interface (IPMI)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Intelligent-Platform-Management-Interface-IPMI)

  IPMI is a standardized computer system interface used by system administrators for out-of-band management of computer systems and monitoring of their operation. In layman’s terms, it is a way to manage a computer using a direct network connection, whether it is turned on or not; connecting to the hardware rather than an operating system or login shell.

- interface[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-interface)

  A physical or virtual device that provides connectivity to another device or medium.

- interface ID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-interface-ID)

  Unique ID for a Networking VIF or vNIC in the form of a UUID.

- Internet Control Message Protocol (ICMP)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Internet-Control-Message-Protocol-ICMP)

  A network protocol used by network devices for control messages. For example, **ping** uses ICMP to test connectivity.

- Internet protocol (IP)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Internet-protocol-IP)

  Principal communications protocol in the internet protocol suite for relaying datagrams across network boundaries.

- Internet Service Provider (ISP)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Internet-Service-Provider-ISP)

  Any business that provides Internet access to individuals or businesses.

- Internet Small Computer System Interface (iSCSI)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Internet-Small-Computer-System-Interface-iSCSI)

  Storage protocol that encapsulates SCSI frames for transport over IP networks. Supported by Compute, Object Storage, and Image service.

- IO[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-IO)

  The abbreviation for input and output.

- IP address[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-IP-address)

  Number that is unique to every computer system on the Internet. Two versions of the Internet Protocol (IP) are in use for addresses: IPv4 and IPv6.

- IP Address Management (IPAM)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-IP-Address-Management-IPAM)

  The process of automating IP address allocation, deallocation, and management. Currently provided by Compute, melange, and Networking.

- ip6tables[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-ip6tables)

  Tool used to set up, maintain, and inspect the tables of IPv6 packet filter rules in the Linux kernel. In OpenStack Compute, ip6tables is used along with arptables, ebtables, and iptables to create firewalls for both nodes and VMs.

- ipset[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-ipset)

  Extension to iptables that allows creation of firewall rules that match entire “sets” of IP addresses simultaneously. These sets reside in indexed data structures to increase efficiency, particularly on systems with a large quantity of rules.

- iptables[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-iptables)

  Used along with arptables and ebtables, iptables create firewalls in Compute. iptables are the tables provided by the Linux kernel firewall (implemented as different Netfilter modules) and the chains and rules it stores. Different kernel modules and programs are currently used for different protocols: iptables applies to IPv4, ip6tables to IPv6, arptables to ARP, and ebtables to Ethernet frames. Requires root privilege to manipulate.

- ironic[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-ironic)

  Codename for the [Bare Metal service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Bare-Metal-service-ironic).

- iSCSI Qualified Name (IQN)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-iSCSI-Qualified-Name-IQN)

  IQN is the format most commonly used for iSCSI names, which uniquely identify nodes in an iSCSI network. All IQNs follow the pattern iqn.yyyy-mm.domain:identifier, where ‘yyyy-mm’ is the year and month in which the domain was registered, ‘domain’ is the reversed domain name of the issuing organization, and ‘identifier’ is an optional string which makes each IQN under the same domain unique. For example, ‘iqn.2015-10.org.openstack.408ae959bce1’.

- ISO9660[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-ISO9660)

  One of the VM image disk formats supported by Image service.

- itsec[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-itsec)

  A default role in the Compute RBAC system that can quarantine an instance in any project.

## J[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#j)

- Java[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Java)

  A programming language that is used to create systems that involve more than one computer by way of a network.

- JavaScript[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-JavaScript)

  A scripting language that is used to build web pages.

- JavaScript Object Notation (JSON)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-JavaScript-Object-Notation-JSON)

  One of the supported response formats in OpenStack.

- jumbo frame[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-jumbo-frame)

  Feature in modern Ethernet networks that supports frames up to approximately 9000 bytes.

- Juno[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Juno)

  The code name for the tenth release of OpenStack. The design summit took place in Atlanta, Georgia, US and Juno is an unincorporated community in Georgia.

## K[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#k)

- Kerberos[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Kerberos)

  A network authentication protocol which works on the basis of tickets. Kerberos allows nodes communication over a non-secure network, and allows nodes to prove their identity to one another in a secure manner.

- kernel-based VM (KVM)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-kernel-based-VM-KVM)

  An OpenStack-supported hypervisor. KVM is a full virtualization solution for Linux on x86 hardware containing virtualization extensions (Intel VT or AMD-V), ARM, IBM Power, and IBM zSeries. It consists of a loadable kernel module, that provides the core virtualization infrastructure and a processor specific module.

- Key Manager service (barbican)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Key-Manager-service-barbican)

  The project that produces a secret storage and generation system capable of providing key management for services wishing to enable encryption features.

- keystone[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-keystone)

  Codename of the [Identity service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Identity-service-keystone).

- Kickstart[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Kickstart)

  A tool to automate system configuration and installation on Red Hat, Fedora, and CentOS-based Linux distributions.

- Kilo[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Kilo)

  The code name for the eleventh release of OpenStack. The design summit took place in Paris, France. Due to delays in the name selection, the release was known only as K. Because `k` is the unit symbol for kilo and the kilogram reference artifact is stored near Paris in the Pavillon de Breteuil in Sèvres, the community chose Kilo as the release name.

## L[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#l)

- large object[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-large-object)

  An object within Object Storage that is larger than 5 GB.

- Launchpad[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Launchpad)

  The collaboration site for OpenStack.

- Layer-2 (L2) agent[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Layer-2-L2-agent)

  OpenStack Networking agent that provides layer-2 connectivity for virtual networks.

- Layer-2 network[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Layer-2-network)

  Term used in the OSI network architecture for the data link layer. The data link layer is responsible for media access control, flow control and detecting and possibly correcting errors that may occur in the physical layer.

- Layer-3 (L3) agent[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Layer-3-L3-agent)

  OpenStack Networking agent that provides layer-3 (routing) services for virtual networks.

- Layer-3 network[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Layer-3-network)

  Term used in the OSI network architecture for the network layer. The network layer is responsible for packet forwarding including routing from one node to another.

- Liberty[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Liberty)

  The code name for the twelfth release of OpenStack. The design summit took place in Vancouver, Canada and Liberty is the name of a village in the Canadian province of Saskatchewan.

- libvirt[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-libvirt)

  Virtualization API library used by OpenStack to interact with many of its supported hypervisors.

- Lightweight Directory Access Protocol (LDAP)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Lightweight-Directory-Access-Protocol-LDAP)

  An application protocol for accessing and maintaining distributed directory information services over an IP network.

- Linux[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Linux)

  Unix-like computer operating system assembled under the model of free and open-source software development and distribution.

- Linux bridge[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Linux-bridge)

  Software that enables multiple VMs to share a single physical NIC within Compute.

- Linux Bridge neutron plug-in[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Linux-Bridge-neutron-plug-in)

  Enables a Linux bridge to understand a Networking port, interface attachment, and other abstractions.

- Linux containers (LXC)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Linux-containers-LXC)

  An OpenStack-supported hypervisor.

- live migration[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-live-migration)

  The ability within Compute to move running virtual machine instances from one host to another with only a small service interruption during switchover.

- load balancer[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-load-balancer)

  A load balancer is a logical device that belongs to a cloud account. It is used to distribute workloads between multiple back-end systems or services, based on the criteria defined as part of its configuration.

- load balancing[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-load-balancing)

  The process of spreading client requests between two or more nodes to improve performance and availability.

- Load-Balancer-as-a-Service (LBaaS)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Load-Balancer-as-a-Service-LBaaS)

  Enables Networking to distribute incoming requests evenly between designated instances.

- Load-balancing service (octavia)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Load-balancing-service-octavia)

  The project that aims to provide scalable, on demand, self service access to load-balancer services, in technology-agnostic manner.

- Logical Volume Manager (LVM)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Logical-Volume-Manager-LVM)

  Provides a method of allocating space on mass-storage devices that is more flexible than conventional partitioning schemes.

## M[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#m)

- magnum[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-magnum)

  Code name for the [Containers Infrastructure Management service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Container-Infrastructure-Management-service-magnum).

- management API[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-management-API)

  Alternative term for an admin API.

- management network[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-management-network)

  A network segment used for administration, not accessible to the public Internet.

- manager[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-manager)

  Logical groupings of related code, such as the Block Storage volume manager or network manager.

- manifest[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-manifest)

  Used to track segments of a large object within Object Storage.

- manifest object[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-manifest-object)

  A special Object Storage object that contains the manifest for a large object.

- manila[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-manila)

  Codename for OpenStack [Shared File Systems service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Shared-File-Systems-service-manila).

- manila-share[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-manila-share)

  Responsible for managing Shared File System Service devices, specifically the back-end devices.

- maximum transmission unit (MTU)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-maximum-transmission-unit-MTU)

  Maximum frame or packet size for a particular network medium. Typically 1500 bytes for Ethernet networks.

- mechanism driver[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-mechanism-driver)

  A driver for the Modular Layer 2 (ML2) neutron plug-in that provides layer-2 connectivity for virtual instances. A single OpenStack installation can use multiple mechanism drivers.

- melange[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-melange)

  Project name for OpenStack Network Information Service. To be merged with Networking.

- membership[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-membership)

  The association between an Image service VM image and a project. Enables images to be shared with specified projects.

- membership list[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-membership-list)

  A list of projects that can access a given VM image within Image service.

- memcached[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-memcached)

  A distributed memory object caching system that is used by Object Storage for caching.

- memory overcommit[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-memory-overcommit)

  The ability to start new VM instances based on the actual memory usage of a host, as opposed to basing the decision on the amount of RAM each running instance thinks it has available. Also known as RAM overcommit.

- message broker[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-message-broker)

  The software package used to provide AMQP messaging capabilities within Compute. Default package is RabbitMQ.

- message bus[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-message-bus)

  The main virtual communication line used by all AMQP messages for inter-cloud communications within Compute.

- message queue[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-message-queue)

  Passes requests from clients to the appropriate workers and returns the output to the client after the job completes.

- Message service (zaqar)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Message-service-zaqar)

  The project that provides a messaging service that affords a variety of distributed application patterns in an efficient, scalable, and highly available manner, and to create and maintain associated Python libraries and documentation.

- Meta-Data Server (MDS)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Meta-Data-Server-MDS)

  Stores CephFS metadata.

- Metadata agent[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Metadata-agent)

  OpenStack Networking agent that provides metadata services for instances.

- migration[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-migration)

  The process of moving a VM instance from one host to another.

- mistral[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-mistral)

  Code name for [Workflow service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Workflow-service-mistral).

- Mitaka[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Mitaka)

  The code name for the thirteenth release of OpenStack. The design summit took place in Tokyo, Japan. Mitaka is a city in Tokyo.

- Modular Layer 2 (ML2) neutron plug-in[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Modular-Layer-2-ML2-neutron-plug-in)

  Can concurrently use multiple layer-2 networking technologies, such as 802.1Q and VXLAN, in Networking.

- monasca[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-monasca)

  Codename for OpenStack [Monitoring](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Monitoring-monasca).

- Monitor (LBaaS)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Monitor-LBaaS)

  LBaaS feature that provides availability monitoring using the `ping` command, TCP, and HTTP/HTTPS GET.

- Monitor (Mon)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Monitor-Mon)

  A Ceph component that communicates with external clients, checks data state and consistency, and performs quorum functions.

- Monitoring (monasca)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Monitoring-monasca)

  The OpenStack service that provides a multi-project, highly scalable, performant, fault-tolerant monitoring-as-a-service solution for metrics, complex event processing and logging. To build an extensible platform for advanced monitoring services that can be used by both operators and projects to gain operational insight and visibility, ensuring availability and stability.

- multi-cloud computing[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-multi-cloud-computing)

  The use of multiple cloud computing and storage services in a single network architecture.

- multi-cloud SDKs[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-multi-cloud-SDKs)

  SDKs that provide a multi-cloud abstraction layer and include support for OpenStack. These SDKs are excellent for writing applications that need to consume more than one type of cloud provider, but may expose a more limited set of features.

- multi-factor authentication[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-multi-factor-authentication)

  Authentication method that uses two or more credentials, such as a password and a private key. Currently not supported in Identity.

- multi-host[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-multi-host)

  High-availability mode for legacy (nova) networking. Each compute node handles NAT and DHCP and acts as a gateway for all of the VMs on it. A networking failure on one compute node doesn’t affect VMs on other compute nodes.

- multinic[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-multinic)

  Facility in Compute that allows each virtual machine instance to have more than one VIF connected to it.

- murano[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-murano)

  Codename for the [Application Catalog service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Application-Catalog-service-murano).

## N[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#n)

- Nebula[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Nebula)

  Released as open source by NASA in 2010 and is the basis for Compute.

- netadmin[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-netadmin)

  One of the default roles in the Compute RBAC system. Enables the user to allocate publicly accessible IP addresses to instances and change firewall rules.

- NetApp volume driver[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-NetApp-volume-driver)

  Enables Compute to communicate with NetApp storage devices through the NetApp OnCommand Provisioning Manager.

- network[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-network)

  A virtual network that provides connectivity between entities. For example, a collection of virtual ports that share network connectivity. In Networking terminology, a network is always a layer-2 network.

- Network Address Translation (NAT)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Network-Address-Translation-NAT)

  Process of modifying IP address information while in transit. Supported by Compute and Networking.

- network controller[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-network-controller)

  A Compute daemon that orchestrates the network configuration of nodes, including IP addresses, VLANs, and bridging. Also manages routing for both public and private networks.

- Network File System (NFS)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Network-File-System-NFS)

  A method for making file systems available over the network. Supported by OpenStack.

- network ID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-network-ID)

  Unique ID assigned to each network segment within Networking. Same as network UUID.

- network manager[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-network-manager)

  The Compute component that manages various network components, such as firewall rules, IP address allocation, and so on.

- network namespace[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-network-namespace)

  Linux kernel feature that provides independent virtual networking instances on a single host with separate routing tables and interfaces. Similar to virtual routing and forwarding (VRF) services on physical network equipment.

- network node[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-network-node)

  Any compute node that runs the network worker daemon.

- network segment[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-network-segment)

  Represents a virtual, isolated OSI layer-2 subnet in Networking.

- Network Service Header (NSH)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Network-Service-Header-NSH)

  Provides a mechanism for metadata exchange along the instantiated service path.

- Network Time Protocol (NTP)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Network-Time-Protocol-NTP)

  Method of keeping a clock for a host or node correct via communication with a trusted, accurate time source.

- network UUID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-network-UUID)

  Unique ID for a Networking network segment.

- network worker[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-network-worker)

  The `nova-network` worker daemon; provides services such as giving an IP address to a booting nova instance.

- Networking API (Neutron API)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Networking-API-Neutron-API)

  API used to access OpenStack Networking. Provides an extensible architecture to enable custom plug-in creation.

- Networking service (neutron)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Networking-service-neutron)

  The OpenStack project which implements services and associated libraries to provide on-demand, scalable, and technology-agnostic network abstraction.

- neutron[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-neutron)

  Codename for OpenStack [Networking service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Networking-service-neutron).

- neutron API[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-neutron-API)

  An alternative name for [Networking API](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Networking-API-Neutron-API).

- neutron manager[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-neutron-manager)

  Enables Compute and Networking integration, which enables Networking to perform network management for guest VMs.

- neutron plug-in[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-neutron-plug-in)

  Interface within Networking that enables organizations to create custom plug-ins for advanced features, such as QoS, ACLs, or IDS.

- Newton[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Newton)

  The code name for the fourteenth release of OpenStack. The design summit took place in Austin, Texas, US. The release is named after “Newton House” which is located at 1013 E. Ninth St., Austin, TX. which is listed on the National Register of Historic Places.

- Nexenta volume driver[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Nexenta-volume-driver)

  Provides support for NexentaStor devices in Compute.

- NFV Orchestration service (tacker)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-NFV-Orchestration-service-tacker)

  OpenStack service that aims to implement Network Function Virtualization (NFV) orchestration services and libraries for end-to-end life-cycle management of network services and Virtual Network Functions (VNFs).

- Nginx[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Nginx)

  An HTTP and reverse proxy server, a mail proxy server, and a generic TCP/UDP proxy server.

- No ACK[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-No-ACK)

  Disables server-side message acknowledgment in the Compute RabbitMQ. Increases performance but decreases reliability.

- node[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-node)

  A VM instance that runs on a host.

- non-durable exchange[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-non-durable-exchange)

  Message exchange that is cleared when the service restarts. Its data is not written to persistent storage.

- non-durable queue[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-non-durable-queue)

  Message queue that is cleared when the service restarts. Its data is not written to persistent storage.

- non-persistent volume[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-non-persistent-volume)

  Alternative term for an ephemeral volume.

- north-south traffic[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-north-south-traffic)

  Network traffic between a user or client (north) and a server (south), or traffic into the cloud (south) and out of the cloud (north). See also east-west traffic.

- nova[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-nova)

  Codename for OpenStack [Compute service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Compute-service-nova).

- Nova API[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Nova-API)

  Alternative term for the [Compute API](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Compute-API-nova-API).

- nova-network[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-nova-network)

  A Compute component that manages IP address allocation, firewalls, and other network-related tasks. This is the legacy networking option and an alternative to Networking.

## O[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#o)

- object[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-object)

  A BLOB of data held by Object Storage; can be in any format.

- object auditor[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-object-auditor)

  Opens all objects for an object server and verifies the MD5 hash, size, and metadata for each object.

- object expiration[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-object-expiration)

  A configurable option within Object Storage to automatically delete objects after a specified amount of time has passed or a certain date is reached.

- object hash[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-object-hash)

  Unique ID for an Object Storage object.

- object path hash[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-object-path-hash)

  Used by Object Storage to determine the location of an object in the ring. Maps objects to partitions.

- object replicator[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-object-replicator)

  An Object Storage component that copies an object to remote partitions for fault tolerance.

- object server[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-object-server)

  An Object Storage component that is responsible for managing objects.

- Object Storage API[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Object-Storage-API)

  API used to access OpenStack [Object Storage](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Object-Storage-service-swift).

- Object Storage Device (OSD)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Object-Storage-Device-OSD)

  The Ceph storage daemon.

- Object Storage service (swift)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Object-Storage-service-swift)

  The OpenStack core project that provides eventually consistent and redundant storage and retrieval of fixed digital content.

- object versioning[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-object-versioning)

  Allows a user to set a flag on an [Object Storage](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Object-Storage-service-swift) container so that all objects within the container are versioned.

- Ocata[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Ocata)

  The code name for the fifteenth release of OpenStack. The design summit took place in Barcelona, Spain. Ocata is a beach north of Barcelona.

- Octavia[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Octavia)

  Code name for the [Load-balancing service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Load-balancing-service-octavia).

- Oldie[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Oldie)

  Term for an [Object Storage](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Object-Storage-service-swift) process that runs for a long time.  Can indicate a hung process.

- Open Cloud Computing Interface (OCCI)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Open-Cloud-Computing-Interface-OCCI)

  A standardized interface for managing compute, data, and network resources, currently unsupported in OpenStack.

- Open Virtualization Format (OVF)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Open-Virtualization-Format-OVF)

  Standard for packaging VM images. Supported in OpenStack.

- Open vSwitch[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Open-vSwitch)

  Open vSwitch is a production quality, multilayer virtual switch licensed under the open source Apache 2.0 license. It is designed to enable massive network automation through programmatic extension, while still supporting standard management interfaces and protocols (for example NetFlow, sFlow, SPAN, RSPAN, CLI, LACP, 802.1ag).

- Open vSwitch (OVS) agent[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Open-vSwitch-OVS-agent)

  Provides an interface to the underlying Open vSwitch service for the Networking plug-in.

- Open vSwitch neutron plug-in[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Open-vSwitch-neutron-plug-in)

  Provides support for Open vSwitch in Networking.

- OpenDev[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-OpenDev)

  [OpenDev](https://opendev.org) is a space for collaborative Open Source software development. OpenDev’s mission is to provide project hosting, continuous integration tooling, and virtual collaboration spaces for Open Source software projects. OpenDev is itself self hosted on this set of tools including code review, continuous integration, etherpad, wiki, code browsing and so on. This means that OpenDev itself is run like an open source project, you can join us and help run the system. Additionally, all of the services run are Open Source software themselves. The OpenStack project is the largest project using OpenDev.

- OpenLDAP[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-OpenLDAP)

  An open source LDAP server. Supported by both Compute and Identity.

- OpenStack[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-OpenStack)

  OpenStack is a cloud operating system that controls large pools of compute, storage, and networking resources throughout a data center, all managed through a dashboard that gives administrators control while empowering their users to provision resources through a web interface. OpenStack is an open source project licensed under the Apache License 2.0.

- OpenStack code name[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-OpenStack-code-name)

  Each OpenStack release has a code name. Code names ascend in alphabetical order: Austin, Bexar, Cactus, Diablo, Essex, Folsom, Grizzly, Havana, Icehouse, Juno, Kilo, Liberty, Mitaka, Newton, Ocata, Pike, Queens, Rocky, Stein, Train, Ussuri, Victoria, Wallaby, Xena, Yoga, Zed. Wallaby was the first code name choosen by a new policy: Code names are choosen by the community following the alphabet, for details see [release name criteria](https://governance.openstack.org/tc/reference/release-naming.html#release-name-criteria). The Victoria name was the last name where code names are cities or counties near where the corresponding OpenStack design summit took place. An exception, called the Waldon exception, was granted to elements of the state flag that sound especially cool. Code names are chosen by popular vote. At the same time as OpenStack releases run out of alphabet the Technical Committee changed the [naming process](https://governance.openstack.org/tc/resolutions/20220524-release-identification-process.html) to have release number and a release name as an identification code. The release number will be the primary identifier: “year”.”release count within the year” and the name will be used mostly for marketing purposes. The first such release is 2023.1 Antelope. Followed by, respectively, 2023.2 Bobcat.

- openSUSE[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-openSUSE)

  A Linux distribution that is compatible with OpenStack.

- operator[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-operator)

  The person responsible for planning and maintaining an OpenStack installation.

- optional service[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-optional-service)

  An official OpenStack service defined as optional by Interop Working Group. Currently, consists of Dashboard (horizon), Telemetry service (Telemetry), Orchestration service (heat), Database service (trove), Bare Metal service (ironic), and so on.

- Orchestration service (heat)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Orchestration-service-heat)

  The OpenStack service which orchestrates composite cloud applications using a declarative template format through an OpenStack-native REST API.

- orphan[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-orphan)

  In the context of Object Storage, this is a process that is not terminated after an upgrade, restart, or reload of the service.

- Oslo[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Oslo)

  Codename for the [Common Libraries project](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Common-Libraries-oslo).

## P[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#p)

- panko[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-panko)

  Part of the OpenStack [Telemetry service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Telemetry-service-telemetry); provides event storage.

- parent cell[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-parent-cell)

  If a requested resource, such as CPU time, disk storage, or memory, is not available in the parent cell, the request is forwarded to associated child cells.

- partition[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-partition)

  A unit of storage within Object Storage used to store objects. It exists on top of devices and is replicated for fault tolerance.

- partition index[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-partition-index)

  Contains the locations of all Object Storage partitions within the ring.

- partition shift value[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-partition-shift-value)

  Used by Object Storage to determine which partition data should reside on.

- path MTU discovery (PMTUD)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-path-MTU-discovery-PMTUD)

  Mechanism in IP networks to detect end-to-end MTU and adjust packet size accordingly.

- pause[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-pause)

  A VM state where no changes occur (no changes in memory, network communications stop, etc); the VM is frozen but not shut down.

- PCI passthrough[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-PCI-passthrough)

  Gives guest VMs exclusive access to a PCI device. Currently supported in OpenStack Havana and later releases.

- persistent message[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-persistent-message)

  A message that is stored both in memory and on disk. The message is not lost after a failure or restart.

- persistent volume[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-persistent-volume)

  Changes to these types of disk volumes are saved.

- personality file[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-personality-file)

  A file used to customize a Compute instance. It can be used to inject SSH keys or a specific network configuration.

- Pike[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Pike)

  The code name for the sixteenth release of OpenStack. The OpenStack summit took place in Boston, Massachusetts, US. The release is named after the Massachusetts Turnpike, abbreviated commonly as the Mass Pike, which is the easternmost stretch of Interstate 90.

- Platform-as-a-Service (PaaS)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Platform-as-a-Service-PaaS)

  Provides to the consumer an operating system and, often, a language runtime and libraries (collectively, the “platform”) upon which they can run their own application code, without providing any control over the underlying infrastructure. Examples of Platform-as-a-Service providers include Cloud Foundry and OpenShift.

- plug-in[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-plug-in)

  Software component providing the actual implementation for Networking APIs, or for Compute APIs, depending on the context.

- policy service[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-policy-service)

  Component of Identity that provides a rule-management interface and a rule-based authorization engine.

- policy-based routing (PBR)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-policy-based-routing-PBR)

  Provides a mechanism to implement packet forwarding and routing according to the policies defined by the network administrator.

- pool[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-pool)

  A logical set of devices, such as web servers, that you group together to receive and process traffic. The load balancing function chooses which member of the pool handles the new requests or connections received on the VIP address. Each VIP has one pool.

- pool member[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-pool-member)

  An application that runs on the back-end server in a load-balancing system.

- port[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-port)

  A virtual network port within Networking; VIFs / vNICs are connected to a port.

- port UUID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-port-UUID)

  Unique ID for a Networking port.

- preseed[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-preseed)

  A tool to automate system configuration and installation on Debian-based Linux distributions.

- private cloud[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-private-cloud)

  Computing resources used exclusively by one business or organization.

- private image[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-private-image)

  An Image service VM image that is only available to specified projects.

- private IP address[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-private-IP-address)

  An IP address used for management and administration, not available to the public Internet.

- private network[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-private-network)

  The Network Controller provides virtual networks to enable compute servers to interact with each other and with the public network. All machines must have a public and private network interface. A private network interface can be a flat or VLAN network interface. A flat network interface is controlled by the flat_interface with flat managers. A VLAN network interface is controlled by the `vlan_interface` option with VLAN managers.

- project[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-project)

  Projects represent the base unit of “ownership” in OpenStack, in that all resources in OpenStack should be owned by a specific project. In OpenStack Identity, a project must be owned by a specific domain.

- project ID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-project-ID)

  Unique ID assigned to each project by the Identity service.

- project VPN[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-project-VPN)

  Alternative term for a cloudpipe.

- promiscuous mode[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-promiscuous-mode)

  Causes the network interface to pass all traffic it receives to the host rather than passing only the frames addressed to it.

- protected property[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-protected-property)

  Generally, extra properties on an Image service image to which only cloud administrators have access. Limits which user roles can perform CRUD operations on that property. The cloud administrator can configure any image property as protected.

- provider[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-provider)

  An administrator who has access to all hosts and instances.

- proxy node[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-proxy-node)

  A node that provides the Object Storage proxy service.

- proxy server[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-proxy-server)

  Users of Object Storage interact with the service through the proxy server, which in turn looks up the location of the requested data within the ring and returns the results to the user.

- public API[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-public-API)

  An API endpoint used for both service-to-service communication and end-user interactions.

- public cloud[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-public-cloud)

  Data centers available to many users over the Internet.

- public image[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-public-image)

  An Image service VM image that is available to all projects.

- public IP address[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-public-IP-address)

  An IP address that is accessible to end-users.

- public key authentication[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-public-key-authentication)

  Authentication method that uses keys rather than passwords.

- public network[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-public-network)

  The Network Controller provides virtual networks to enable compute servers to interact with each other and with the public network. All machines must have a public and private network interface. The public network interface is controlled by the `public_interface` option.

- Puppet[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Puppet)

  An operating system configuration-management tool supported by OpenStack.

- Python[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Python)

  Programming language used extensively in OpenStack.

## Q[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#q)

- QEMU Copy On Write 2 (QCOW2)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-QEMU-Copy-On-Write-2-QCOW2)

  One of the VM image disk formats supported by Image service.

- Qpid[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Qpid)

  Message queue software supported by OpenStack; an alternative to RabbitMQ.

- Quality of Service (QoS)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Quality-of-Service-QoS)

  The ability to guarantee certain network or storage requirements to satisfy a Service Level Agreement (SLA) between an application provider and end users. Typically includes performance requirements like networking bandwidth, latency, jitter correction, and reliability as well as storage performance in Input/Output Operations Per Second (IOPS), throttling agreements, and performance expectations at peak load.

- quarantine[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-quarantine)

  If Object Storage finds objects, containers, or accounts that are corrupt, they are placed in this state, are not replicated, cannot be read by clients, and a correct copy is re-replicated.

- Queens[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Queens)

  The code name for the seventeenth release of OpenStack. The OpenStack summit took place in Sydney, Australia. The release is named after the Queens Pound river in the South Coast region of New South Wales.

- Quick EMUlator (QEMU)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Quick-EMUlator-QEMU)

  QEMU is a generic and open source machine emulator and virtualizer. One of the hypervisors supported by OpenStack, generally used for development purposes.

- quota[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-quota)

  In Compute and Block Storage, the ability to set resource limits on a per-project basis.

## R[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#r)

- RabbitMQ[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-RabbitMQ)

  The default message queue software used by OpenStack.

- Rackspace Cloud Files[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Rackspace-Cloud-Files)

  Released as open source by Rackspace in 2010; the basis for Object Storage.

- RADOS Block Device (RBD)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-RADOS-Block-Device-RBD)

  Ceph component that enables a Linux block device to be striped over multiple distributed data stores.

- radvd[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-radvd)

  The router advertisement daemon, used by the Compute VLAN manager and FlatDHCP manager to provide routing services for VM instances.

- rally[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-rally)

  Codename for the [Benchmark service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Benchmark-service-rally).

- RAM filter[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-RAM-filter)

  The Compute setting that enables or disables RAM overcommitment.

- RAM overcommit[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-RAM-overcommit)

  The ability to start new VM instances based on the actual memory usage of a host, as opposed to basing the decision on the amount of RAM each running instance thinks it has available. Also known as memory overcommit.

- rate limit[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-rate-limit)

  Configurable option within Object Storage to limit database writes on a per-account and/or per-container basis.

- raw[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-raw)

  One of the VM image disk formats supported by Image service; an unstructured disk image.

- rebalance[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-rebalance)

  The process of distributing Object Storage partitions across all drives in the ring; used during initial ring creation and after ring reconfiguration.

- reboot[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-reboot)

  Either a soft or hard reboot of a server. With a soft reboot, the operating system is signaled to restart, which enables a graceful shutdown of all processes. A hard reboot is the equivalent of power cycling the server. The virtualization platform should ensure that the reboot action has completed successfully, even in cases in which the underlying domain/VM is paused or halted/stopped.

- rebuild[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-rebuild)

  Removes all data on the server and replaces it with the specified image. Server ID and IP addresses remain the same.

- Recon[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Recon)

  An Object Storage component that collects meters.

- record[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-record)

  Belongs to a particular domain and is used to specify information about the domain. There are several types of DNS records. Each record type contains particular information used to describe the purpose of that record. Examples include mail exchange (MX) records, which specify the mail server for a particular domain; and name server (NS) records, which specify the authoritative name servers for a domain.

- record ID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-record-ID)

  A number within a database that is incremented each time a change is made. Used by Object Storage when replicating.

- Red Hat Enterprise Linux (RHEL)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Red-Hat-Enterprise-Linux-RHEL)

  A Linux distribution that is compatible with OpenStack.

- reference architecture[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-reference-architecture)

  A recommended architecture for an OpenStack cloud.

- region[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-region)

  A discrete OpenStack environment with dedicated API endpoints that typically shares only the Identity (keystone) with other regions.

- registry[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-registry)

  Alternative term for the Image service registry.

- registry server[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-registry-server)

  An Image service that provides VM image metadata information to clients.

- Reliable, Autonomic Distributed Object Store[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Reliable-Autonomic-Distributed-Object-Store)

  (RADOS) A collection of components that provides object storage within Ceph. Similar to OpenStack Object Storage.

- Remote Procedure Call (RPC)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Remote-Procedure-Call-RPC)

  The method used by the Compute RabbitMQ for intra-service communications.

- replica[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-replica)

  Provides data redundancy and fault tolerance by creating copies of Object Storage objects, accounts, and containers so that they are not lost when the underlying storage fails.

- replica count[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-replica-count)

  The number of replicas of the data in an Object Storage ring.

- replication[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-replication)

  The process of copying data to a separate physical device for fault tolerance and performance.

- replicator[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-replicator)

  The Object Storage back-end process that creates and manages object replicas.

- request ID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-request-ID)

  Unique ID assigned to each request sent to Compute.

- rescue image[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-rescue-image)

  A special type of VM image that is booted when an instance is placed into rescue mode. Allows an administrator to mount the file systems for an instance to correct the problem.

- resize[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-resize)

  Converts an existing server to a different flavor, which scales the server up or down. The original server is saved to enable rollback if a problem occurs. All resizes must be tested and explicitly confirmed, at which time the original server is removed.

- RESTful[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-RESTful)

  A kind of web service API that uses REST, or Representational State Transfer. REST is the style of architecture for hypermedia systems that is used for the World Wide Web.

- ring[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-ring)

  An entity that maps Object Storage data to partitions. A separate ring exists for each service, such as account, object, and container.

- ring builder[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-ring-builder)

  Builds and manages rings within Object Storage, assigns partitions to devices, and pushes the configuration to other storage nodes.

- Rocky[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Rocky)

  The code name for the eightteenth release of OpenStack. The OpenStack summit took place in Vancouver, Canada. The release is named after the Rocky Mountains.

- role[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-role)

  A personality that a user assumes to perform a specific set of operations. A role includes a set of rights and privileges. A user assuming that role inherits those rights and privileges.

- Role Based Access Control (RBAC)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Role-Based-Access-Control-RBAC)

  Provides a predefined list of actions that the user can perform, such as start or stop VMs, reset passwords, and so on. Supported in both Identity and Compute and can be configured using the dashboard.

- role ID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-role-ID)

  Alphanumeric ID assigned to each Identity service role.

- Root Cause Analysis (RCA) service (Vitrage)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Root-Cause-Analysis-RCA-service-Vitrage)

  OpenStack project that aims to organize, analyze and visualize OpenStack alarms and events, yield insights regarding the root cause of problems and deduce their existence before they are directly detected.

- rootwrap[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-rootwrap)

  A feature of Compute that allows the unprivileged “nova” user to run a specified list of commands as the Linux root user.

- round-robin scheduler[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-round-robin-scheduler)

  Type of Compute scheduler that evenly distributes instances among available hosts.

- router[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-router)

  A physical or virtual network device that passes network traffic between different networks.

- routing key[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-routing-key)

  The Compute direct exchanges, fanout exchanges, and topic exchanges use this key to determine how to process a message; processing varies depending on exchange type.

- RPC driver[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-RPC-driver)

  Modular system that allows the underlying message queue software of Compute to be changed. For example, from RabbitMQ to ZeroMQ or Qpid.

- rsync[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-rsync)

  Used by Object Storage to push object replicas.

- RXTX cap[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-RXTX-cap)

  Absolute limit on the amount of network traffic a Compute VM instance can send and receive.

- RXTX quota[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-RXTX-quota)

  Soft limit on the amount of network traffic a Compute VM instance can send and receive.

## S[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#s)

- sahara[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-sahara)

  Codename for the [Data Processing service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Data-Processing-service-sahara).

- SAML assertion[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-SAML-assertion)

  Contains information about a user as provided by the identity provider. It is an indication that a user has been authenticated.

- Sandbox[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Sandbox)

  A virtual space in which new or untested software can be run securely.

- scheduler manager[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-scheduler-manager)

  A Compute component that determines where VM instances should start. Uses modular design to support a variety of scheduler types.

- scoped token[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-scoped-token)

  An Identity service API access token that is associated with a specific project.

- scrubber[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-scrubber)

  Checks for and deletes unused VMs; the component of Image service that implements delayed delete.

- secret key[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-secret-key)

  String of text known only by the user; used along with an access key to make requests to the Compute API.

- secure boot[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-secure-boot)

  Process whereby the system firmware validates the authenticity of the code involved in the boot process.

- secure shell (SSH)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-secure-shell-SSH)

  Open source tool used to access remote hosts through an encrypted communications channel, SSH key injection is supported by Compute.

- security group[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-security-group)

  A set of network traffic filtering rules that are applied to a Compute instance.

- segmented object[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-segmented-object)

  An Object Storage large object that has been broken up into pieces. The re-assembled object is called a concatenated object.

- self-service[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-self-service)

  For IaaS, ability for a regular (non-privileged) account to manage a virtual infrastructure component such as networks without involving an administrator.

- SELinux[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-SELinux)

  Linux kernel security module that provides the mechanism for supporting access control policies.

- senlin[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-senlin)

  Code name for the [Clustering service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Clustering-service-senlin).

- server[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-server)

  Computer that provides explicit services to the client software running on that system, often managing a variety of computer operations. A server is a VM instance in the Compute system. Flavor and image are requisite elements when creating a server.

- server image[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-server-image)

  Alternative term for a VM image.

- server UUID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-server-UUID)

  Unique ID assigned to each guest VM instance.

- service[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-service)

  An OpenStack service, such as Compute, Object Storage, or Image service. Provides one or more endpoints through which users can access resources and perform operations.

- service catalog[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-service-catalog)

  Alternative term for the Identity service catalog.

- Service Function Chain (SFC)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Service-Function-Chain-SFC)

  For a given service, SFC is the abstracted view of the required service functions and the order in which they are to be applied.

- service ID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-service-ID)

  Unique ID assigned to each service that is available in the Identity service catalog.

- Service Level Agreement (SLA)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Service-Level-Agreement-SLA)

  Contractual obligations that ensure the availability of a service.

- service project[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-service-project)

  Special project that contains all services that are listed in the catalog.

- service provider[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-service-provider)

  A system that provides services to other system entities. In case of federated identity, OpenStack Identity is the service provider.

- service registration[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-service-registration)

  An Identity service feature that enables services, such as Compute, to automatically register with the catalog.

- service token[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-service-token)

  An administrator-defined token used by Compute to communicate securely with the Identity service.

- session back end[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-session-back-end)

  The method of storage used by horizon to track client sessions, such as local memory, cookies, a database, or memcached.

- session persistence[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-session-persistence)

  A feature of the load-balancing service. It attempts to force subsequent connections to a service to be redirected to the same node as long as it is online.

- session storage[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-session-storage)

  A horizon component that stores and tracks client session information. Implemented through the Django sessions framework.

- share[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-share)

  A remote, mountable file system in the context of the [Shared File Systems service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Shared-File-Systems-service-manila). You can mount a share to, and access a share from, several hosts by several users at a time.

- share network[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-share-network)

  An entity in the context of the [Shared File Systems service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Shared-File-Systems-service-manila) that encapsulates interaction with the Networking service. If the driver you selected runs in the mode requiring such kind of interaction, you need to specify the share network to create a share.

- Shared File Systems API[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Shared-File-Systems-API)

  A Shared File Systems service that provides a stable RESTful API. The service authenticates and routes requests throughout the Shared File Systems service. There is python-manilaclient to interact with the API.

- Shared File Systems service (manila)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Shared-File-Systems-service-manila)

  The service that provides a set of services for management of shared file systems in a multi-project cloud environment, similar to how OpenStack provides block-based storage management through the OpenStack [Block Storage service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Block-Storage-service-cinder) project. With the Shared File Systems service, you can create a remote file system and mount the file system on your instances. You can also read and write data from your instances to and from your file system.

- shared IP address[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-shared-IP-address)

  An IP address that can be assigned to a VM instance within the shared IP group. Public IP addresses can be shared across multiple servers for use in various high-availability scenarios. When an IP address is shared to another server, the cloud network restrictions are modified to enable each server to listen to and respond on that IP address. You can optionally specify that the target server network configuration be modified. Shared IP addresses can be used with many standard heartbeat facilities, such as keepalive, that monitor for failure and manage IP failover.

- shared IP group[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-shared-IP-group)

  A collection of servers that can share IPs with other members of the group. Any server in a group can share one or more public IPs with any other server in the group. With the exception of the first server in a shared IP group, servers must be launched into shared IP groups. A server may be a member of only one shared IP group.

- shared storage[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-shared-storage)

  Block storage that is simultaneously accessible by multiple clients, for example, NFS.

- Sheepdog[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Sheepdog)

  Distributed block storage system for QEMU, supported by OpenStack.

- Simple Cloud Identity Management (SCIM)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Simple-Cloud-Identity-Management-SCIM)

  Specification for managing identity in the cloud, currently unsupported by OpenStack.

- Simple Protocol for Independent Computing Environments (SPICE)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Simple-Protocol-for-Independent-Computing-Environments-SPICE)

  SPICE provides remote desktop access to guest virtual machines. It is an alternative to VNC. SPICE is supported by OpenStack.

- Single-root I/O Virtualization (SR-IOV)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Single-root-I-O-Virtualization-SR-IOV)

  A specification that, when implemented by a physical PCIe device, enables it to appear as multiple separate PCIe devices. This enables multiple virtualized guests to share direct access to the physical device, offering improved performance over an equivalent virtual device. Currently supported in OpenStack Havana and later releases.

- SmokeStack[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-SmokeStack)

  Runs automated tests against the core OpenStack API; written in Rails.

- snapshot[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-snapshot)

  A point-in-time copy of an OpenStack storage volume or image. Use storage volume snapshots to back up volumes. Use image snapshots to back up data, or as “gold” images for additional servers.

- soft reboot[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-soft-reboot)

  A controlled reboot where a VM instance is properly restarted through operating system commands.

- Software Development Kit (SDK)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Software-Development-Kit-SDK)

  Contains code, examples, and documentation that you use to create applications in the language of your choice.

- Software Development Lifecycle Automation service (solum)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Software-Development-Lifecycle-Automation-service-solum)

  OpenStack project that aims to make cloud services easier to consume and integrate with application development process by automating the source-to-image process, and simplifying app-centric deployment.

- Software-defined networking (SDN)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Software-defined-networking-SDN)

  Provides an approach for network administrators to manage computer network services through abstraction of lower-level functionality.

- SolidFire Volume Driver[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-SolidFire-Volume-Driver)

  The Block Storage driver for the SolidFire iSCSI storage appliance.

- solum[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-solum)

  Code name for the [Software Development Lifecycle Automation service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Software-Development-Lifecycle-Automation-service-solum).

- spread-first scheduler[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-spread-first-scheduler)

  The Compute VM scheduling algorithm that attempts to start a new VM on the host with the least amount of load.

- SQLAlchemy[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-SQLAlchemy)

  An open source SQL toolkit for Python, used in OpenStack.

- SQLite[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-SQLite)

  A lightweight SQL database, used as the default persistent storage method in many OpenStack services.

- stack[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-stack)

  A set of OpenStack resources created and managed by the Orchestration service according to a given template (either an AWS CloudFormation template or a Heat Orchestration Template (HOT)).

- StackTach[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-StackTach)

  Community project that captures Compute AMQP communications; useful for debugging.

- static IP address[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-static-IP-address)

  Alternative term for a fixed IP address.

- StaticWeb[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-StaticWeb)

  WSGI middleware component of Object Storage that serves container data as a static web page.

- Stein[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Stein)

  The code name for the nineteenth release of OpenStack. The OpenStack Summit took place in Berlin, Germany. The release is named after the street Steinstraße in Berlin.

- storage back end[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-storage-back-end)

  The method that a service uses for persistent storage, such as iSCSI, NFS, or local disk.

- storage manager[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-storage-manager)

  A XenAPI component that provides a pluggable interface to support a wide variety of persistent storage back ends.

- storage manager back end[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-storage-manager-back-end)

  A persistent storage method supported by XenAPI, such as iSCSI or NFS.

- storage node[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-storage-node)

  An Object Storage node that provides container services, account services, and object services; controls the account databases, container databases, and object storage.

- storage services[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-storage-services)

  Collective name for the Object Storage object services, container services, and account services.

- strategy[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-strategy)

  Specifies the authentication source used by Image service or Identity. In the Database service, it refers to the extensions implemented for a data store.

- subdomain[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-subdomain)

  A domain within a parent domain. Subdomains cannot be registered. Subdomains enable you to delegate domains. Subdomains can themselves have subdomains, so third-level, fourth-level, fifth-level, and deeper levels of nesting are possible.

- subnet[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-subnet)

  Logical subdivision of an IP network.

- SUSE Linux Enterprise Server (SLES)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-SUSE-Linux-Enterprise-Server-SLES)

  A Linux distribution that is compatible with OpenStack.

- suspend[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-suspend)

  The VM instance is paused and its state is saved to disk of the host.
