- swap[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-swap)

  Disk-based virtual memory used by operating systems to provide more memory than is actually available on the system.

- swift[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-swift)

  Codename for OpenStack [Object Storage service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Object-Storage-service-swift).

- swift All in One (SAIO)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-swift-All-in-One-SAIO)

  Creates a full Object Storage development environment within a single VM.

- swift middleware[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-swift-middleware)

  Collective term for Object Storage components that provide additional functionality.

- swift proxy server[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-swift-proxy-server)

  Acts as the gatekeeper to Object Storage and is responsible for authenticating the user.

- swift storage node[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-swift-storage-node)

  A node that runs Object Storage account, container, and object services.

- sync point[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-sync-point)

  Point in time since the last container and accounts database sync among nodes within Object Storage.

- sysadmin[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-sysadmin)

  One of the default roles in the Compute RBAC system. Enables a user to add other users to a project, interact with VM images that are associated with the project, and start and stop VM instances.

- system usage[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-system-usage)

  A Compute component that, along with the notification system, collects meters and usage information. This information can be used for billing.

## T[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#t)

- tacker[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-tacker)

  Code name for the [NFV Orchestration service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-NFV-Orchestration-service-tacker)

- Telemetry service (telemetry)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Telemetry-service-telemetry)

  The OpenStack project which collects measurements of the utilization of the physical and virtual resources comprising deployed clouds, persists this data for subsequent retrieval and analysis, and triggers actions when defined criteria are met.

- TempAuth[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-TempAuth)

  An authentication facility within Object Storage that enables Object Storage itself to perform authentication and authorization. Frequently used in testing and development.

- Tempest[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Tempest)

  Automated software test suite designed to run against the trunk of the OpenStack core project.

- TempURL[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-TempURL)

  An Object Storage middleware component that enables creation of URLs for temporary object access.

- tenant[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-tenant)

  A group of users; used to isolate access to Compute resources. An alternative term for a project.

- Tenant API[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Tenant-API)

  An API that is accessible to projects.

- tenant endpoint[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-tenant-endpoint)

  An Identity service API endpoint that is associated with one or more projects.

- tenant ID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-tenant-ID)

  An alternative term for [project ID](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-project-ID).

- token[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-token)

  An alpha-numeric string of text used to access OpenStack APIs and resources.

- token services[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-token-services)

  An Identity service component that manages and validates tokens after a user or project has been authenticated.

- tombstone[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-tombstone)

  Used to mark Object Storage objects that have been deleted; ensures that the object is not updated on another node after it has been deleted.

- topic publisher[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-topic-publisher)

  A process that is created when a RPC call is executed; used to push the message to the topic exchange.

- Torpedo[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Torpedo)

  Community project used to run automated tests against the OpenStack API.

- Train[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Train)

  The code name for the twentieth release of OpenStack. The OpenStack Infrastructure Summit took place in Denver, Colorado, US. Two Project Team Gathering meetings in Denver were held at a hotel next to the train line from downtown to the airport. The crossing signals there had some sort of malfunction in the past causing them to not stop the cars when a train was coming properly. As a result the trains were required to blow their horns when passing through that area. Obviously staying in a hotel, by trains that are blowing their horns 24/7 was less than ideal. As a result, many jokes popped up about Denver and trains - and thus the release is called train.

- transaction ID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-transaction-ID)

  Unique ID assigned to each Object Storage request; used for debugging and tracing.

- transient[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-transient)

  Alternative term for non-durable.

- transient exchange[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-transient-exchange)

  Alternative term for a non-durable exchange.

- transient message[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-transient-message)

  A message that is stored in memory and is lost after the server is restarted.

- transient queue[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-transient-queue)

  Alternative term for a non-durable queue.

- TripleO[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-TripleO)

  OpenStack-on-OpenStack program. The code name for the OpenStack Deployment program.

- trove[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-trove)

  Codename for OpenStack [Database service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Database-service-trove).

- trusted platform module (TPM)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-trusted-platform-module-TPM)

  Specialized microprocessor for incorporating cryptographic keys into devices for authenticating and securing a hardware platform.

## U[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#u)

- Ubuntu[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Ubuntu)

  A Debian-based Linux distribution.

- unscoped token[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-unscoped-token)

  Alternative term for an Identity service default token.

- updater[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-updater)

  Collective term for a group of Object Storage components that processes queued and failed updates for containers and objects.

- user[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-user)

  In OpenStack Identity,  entities represent individual API consumers and are owned by a specific domain. In OpenStack Compute, a user can be associated with roles, projects, or both.

- user data[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-user-data)

  A blob of data that the user can specify when they launch an instance. The instance can access this data through the metadata service or config drive. Commonly used to pass a shell script that the instance runs on boot.

- User Mode Linux (UML)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-User-Mode-Linux-UML)

  An OpenStack-supported hypervisor.

- Ussuri[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Ussuri)

  The code name for the twenty first release of OpenStack. The OpenStack Infrastructure Summit took place in Shanghai, People’s Republic of China. The release is named after the Ussuri river.

## V[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#v)

- Victoria[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Victoria)

  The code name for the twenty second release of OpenStack. The OpenDev + PTG was planned to take place in Vancouver, British Columbia, Canada. The release is named after Victoria, the capital city of British Columbia. The in-person event was cancelled due to COVID-19. The event is being virtualized instead.

- VIF UUID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-VIF-UUID)

  Unique ID assigned to each Networking VIF.

- Virtual Central Processing Unit (vCPU)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Virtual-Central-Processing-Unit-vCPU)

  Subdivides physical CPUs. Instances can then use those divisions.

- Virtual Disk Image (VDI)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Virtual-Disk-Image-VDI)

  One of the VM image disk formats supported by Image service.

- Virtual Extensible LAN (VXLAN)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Virtual-Extensible-LAN-VXLAN)

  A network virtualization technology that attempts to reduce the scalability problems associated with large cloud computing deployments. It uses a VLAN-like encapsulation technique to encapsulate Ethernet frames within UDP packets.

- Virtual Hard Disk (VHD)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Virtual-Hard-Disk-VHD)

  One of the VM image disk formats supported by Image service.

- virtual IP address (VIP)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-virtual-IP-address-VIP)

  An Internet Protocol (IP) address configured on the load balancer for use by clients connecting to a service that is load balanced. Incoming connections are distributed to back-end nodes based on the configuration of the load balancer.

- virtual machine (VM)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-virtual-machine-VM)

  An operating system instance that runs on top of a hypervisor. Multiple VMs can run at the same time on the same physical host.

- virtual network[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-virtual-network)

  An L2 network segment within Networking.

- Virtual Network Computing (VNC)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Virtual-Network-Computing-VNC)

  Open source GUI and CLI tools used for remote console access to VMs. Supported by Compute.

- Virtual Network InterFace (VIF)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Virtual-Network-InterFace-VIF)

  An interface that is plugged into a port in a Networking network. Typically a virtual network interface belonging to a VM.

- virtual networking[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-virtual-networking)

  A generic term for virtualization of network functions such as switching, routing, load balancing, and security using a combination of VMs and overlays on physical network infrastructure.

- virtual port[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-virtual-port)

  Attachment point where a virtual interface connects to a virtual network.

- virtual private network (VPN)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-virtual-private-network-VPN)

  Provided by Compute in the form of cloudpipes, specialized instances that are used to create VPNs on a per-project basis.

- virtual server[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-virtual-server)

  Alternative term for a VM or guest.

- virtual switch (vSwitch)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-virtual-switch-vSwitch)

  Software that runs on a host or node and provides the features and functions of a hardware-based network switch.

- virtual VLAN[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-virtual-VLAN)

  Alternative term for a virtual network.

- VirtualBox[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-VirtualBox)

  An OpenStack-supported hypervisor.

- Vitrage[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Vitrage)

  Code name for the [Root Cause Analysis service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Root-Cause-Analysis-RCA-service-Vitrage).

- VLAN manager[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-VLAN-manager)

  A Compute component that provides dnsmasq and radvd and sets up forwarding to and from cloudpipe instances.

- VLAN network[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-VLAN-network)

  The Network Controller provides virtual networks to enable compute servers to interact with each other and with the public network. All machines must have a public and private network interface. A VLAN network is a private network interface, which is controlled by the `vlan_interface` option with VLAN managers.

- VM disk (VMDK)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-VM-disk-VMDK)

  One of the VM image disk formats supported by Image service.

- VM image[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-VM-image)

  Alternative term for an image.

- VM Remote Control (VMRC)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-VM-Remote-Control-VMRC)

  Method to access VM instance consoles using a web browser. Supported by Compute.

- VMware API[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-VMware-API)

  Supports interaction with VMware products in Compute.

- VMware NSX Neutron plug-in[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-VMware-NSX-Neutron-plug-in)

  Provides support for VMware NSX in Neutron.

- VNC proxy[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-VNC-proxy)

  A Compute component that provides users access to the consoles of their VM instances through VNC or VMRC.

- volume[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-volume)

  Disk-based data storage generally represented as an iSCSI target with a file system that supports extended attributes; can be persistent or ephemeral.

- Volume API[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Volume-API)

  Alternative name for the Block Storage API.

- volume controller[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-volume-controller)

  A Block Storage component that oversees and coordinates storage volume actions.

- volume driver[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-volume-driver)

  Alternative term for a volume plug-in.

- volume ID[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-volume-ID)

  Unique ID applied to each storage volume under the Block Storage control.

- volume manager[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-volume-manager)

  A Block Storage component that creates, attaches, and detaches persistent storage volumes.

- volume node[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-volume-node)

  A Block Storage node that runs the cinder-volume daemon.

- volume plug-in[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-volume-plug-in)

  Provides support for new and specialized types of back-end storage for the Block Storage volume manager.

- volume worker[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-volume-worker)

  A cinder component that interacts with back-end storage to manage the creation and deletion of volumes and the creation of compute volumes, provided by the cinder-volume daemon.

- vSphere[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-vSphere)

  An OpenStack-supported hypervisor.

## W[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#w)

- Wallaby[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Wallaby)

  The code name for the twenty third release of OpenStack. Wallabies are native to Australia, which at the start of this naming period was experiencing unprecedented wild fires.

- Watcher[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Watcher)

  Code name for the [Infrastructure Optimization service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Infrastructure-Optimization-service-watcher).

- weight[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-weight)

  Used by Object Storage devices to determine which storage devices are suitable for the job. Devices are weighted by size.

- weighted cost[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-weighted-cost)

  The sum of each cost used when deciding where to start a new VM instance in Compute.

- weighting[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-weighting)

  A Compute process that determines the suitability of the VM instances for a job for a particular host. For example, not enough RAM on the host, too many CPUs on the host, and so on.

- worker[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-worker)

  A daemon that listens to a queue and carries out tasks in response to messages. For example, the cinder-volume worker manages volume creation and deletion on storage arrays.

- Workflow service (mistral)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Workflow-service-mistral)

  The OpenStack service that provides a simple YAML-based language to write workflows (tasks and transition rules) and a service that allows to upload them, modify, run them at scale and in a highly available manner, manage and monitor workflow execution state and state of individual tasks.

## X[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#x)

- X.509[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-X.509)

  X.509 is the most widely used standard for defining digital certificates. It is a data structure that contains the subject (entity) identifiable information such as its name along with its public key. The certificate can contain a few other attributes as well depending upon the version. The most recent and standard version of X.509 is v3.

- Xen[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Xen)

  Xen is a hypervisor using a microkernel design, providing services that allow multiple computer operating systems to execute on the same computer hardware concurrently.

- Xen API[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Xen-API)

  The Xen administrative API, which is supported by Compute.

- Xen Cloud Platform (XCP)[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Xen-Cloud-Platform-XCP)

  An OpenStack-supported hypervisor.

- Xen Storage Manager Volume Driver[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Xen-Storage-Manager-Volume-Driver)

  A Block Storage volume plug-in that enables communication with the Xen Storage Manager API.

- Xena[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Xena)

  The code name for the twenty fourth release of OpenStack. The release is named after a fictional warrior princess.

- XenServer[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-XenServer)

  An OpenStack-supported hypervisor.

- XFS[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-XFS)

  High-performance 64-bit file system created by Silicon Graphics. Excels in parallel I/O operations and data consistency.

## Y[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#y)

- Yoga[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Yoga)

  The code name for the twenty fifth release of OpenStack. The release is named after a philosophical school with mental and physical practices from India.

## Z[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#z)

- zaqar[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-zaqar)

  Codename for the [Message service](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Message-service-zaqar).

- Zed[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Zed)

  The code name for the twenty sixth release of OpenStack. The release is named after the pronunciation of the letter Z.

- ZeroMQ[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-ZeroMQ)

  Message queue software supported by OpenStack. An alternative to RabbitMQ. Also spelled 0MQ.

- Zuul[¶](https://docs.openstack.org/install-guide/common/glossary.html#term-Zuul)

  [Zuul](https://zuul-ci.org) is an open source CI/CD platform specializing in gating changes across multiple systems and applications before landing a single patch. Zuul is used for OpenStack development to ensure that only tested code gets merged.
